<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>ARTHUR J. GALLAGHER&nbsp;&amp; CO. ANNOUNCES </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>FIRST QUARTER 2021 FINANCIAL RESULTS </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">ROLLING MEADOWS, IL, April&nbsp;29, 2021 &#151; Arthur J. Gallagher&nbsp;&amp; Co. (NYSE: AJG) today reported its financial results for the quarter ended
March&nbsp;31, 2021. Management will host a webcast conference call to discuss these results on Thursday, April&nbsp;29, 2021 at 5:15 p.m. ET/4:15 p.m. CT. To listen to the call, and for printer-friendly formats of this release and the
&#147;Supplemental Quarterly Data&#148; and &#147;CFO Commentary,&#148; which may also be referenced during the call, please visit <U>ajg.com/IR</U>. These documents contain both GAAP and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures.

<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">*</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">For first quarter 2021, the pretax impact of the Brokerage segment adjustments totals $21.8&nbsp;million, with
a corresponding adjustment to the provision for income taxes of $4.6&nbsp;million relating to these items. For first quarter 2021, the pretax impact of the Risk Management segment adjustments totals $3.1&nbsp;million, with a corresponding adjustment
to the provision for income taxes of $0.8&nbsp;million relating to these items. A detailed reconciliation of the 2021 and 2020 provision (benefit) for income taxes is shown on pages 13 and 14. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">(1 of 14) </P>

</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;We are off to an excellent start in 2021,&#148; said J. Patrick Gallagher, Jr., Chairman, President
and CEO. &#147;We posted strong total revenue growth, including excellent organic revenue growth and continued growth from our <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">tuck-in</FONT> M&amp;A strategy. Combined with our expense discipline, we once again
delivered fantastic growth in net earnings and EBITDAC.&#148; </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;We are operating in a firm property casualty environment where rates are up in nearly
all lines and geographies around the globe, which is consistent with the past few quarters. At this time, we don&#146;t see conditions that would indicate this rate environment would change anytime soon. Exposure units also show signs of continued
growth as business activity rebounds and unemployment falls. An increasing rate and exposure unit environment is when our team shines by providing clients with the very best insurance, consulting and risk management advice &#150; and our global team
remains energized. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In addition, we were selected as a World&#146;s Most Ethical Company for the tenth year in a row by the Ethisphere Institute; another
affirmation that our unique culture continues to thrive around the globe. I believe we are very well positioned for the remainder of 2021!&#148; </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19</FONT> Impact </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In our property/casualty Brokerage operations, during first quarter 2021 (a) our customer retention
and new business generation remained similar to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels, (b)&nbsp;renewal exposure units (i.e., insured values, payrolls, employees, miles driven, etc.) were lower than <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> first quarter 2020, but higher than the last three quarters of 2020, (c) premium rates across most geographies and lines of coverage have continued to increase, effectively mitigating exposure unit
declines, and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(d)&nbsp;mid-term</FONT> policy modifications (including cancellations) were a net positive, similar to first quarter 2020. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Thus far in second quarter 2021, property/casualty new business, retentions and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mid-term</FONT> policy modifications are
trending similar to first quarter 2021 and much improved compared to lows seen in April and May 2020, as our customers&#146; businesses continue to recover and economic activity increases. So far during second quarter 2021, we continue to see
overall property/casualty premium rates move higher and exposure units also trended higher than first quarter 2021. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In our employee benefits Brokerage
operations, during first quarter 2021 (a) we saw a slight improvement in covered lives on renewal business compared to fourth quarter 2020, yet still lower than <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels, and (b)&nbsp;new consulting
and special project work was also lower than <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels. So far during second quarter 2021, we are seeing a modest increase in covered lives, consulting engagements and special project work compared
to first quarter 2021. We believe these favorable trends should continue for the remainder of 2021; however, if the economic recovery slows or reverses course, we could see our benefits revenue soften from current levels. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In our Risk Management operations, first quarter 2021 new claims arising were consistent with fourth quarter 2020, but still below <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> first quarter 2020 levels. So far during second quarter 2021, we are seeing new claims arising similar to first quarter 2021, which is a substantial increase compared to lows seen in April and May 2020.
A slower recovery or reversal in the number of workers employed could cause fewer claims to arise in future quarters. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Our clean energy investments saw
higher electricity production in first quarter 2021 compared to first quarter 2020 due to colder temperatures, rising natural gas prices and more plants within our portfolio being operational during the period. First quarter 2021 production was only
slightly lower than <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> production levels seen in first quarter 2019. However, lower overall demand for energy caused by the pandemic and more supply from renewables may cause lower production by the
plants within our portfolio for the remainder of 2021. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Of our nearly 1,000 office locations, more than 400 are open, but most at reduced capacity.
Accordingly, the vast majority of our employees continue to work remotely for some or all of their work week. We believe our service levels are unchanged from <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels. We have not had any
office-wide outbreaks of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19,</FONT> and there have been approximately 450 confirmed cases among approximately 34,000 employees - all of which we believe contracted the virus outside of our office locations.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Given the deterioration in economic conditions since first quarter 2020, we are actively managing costs by limiting discretionary spending such as
travel, entertainment and advertising expenses, adjusting our real estate footprint, reducing capital expenditures, limiting use of outside labor and consultants, increasing utilization of our centers of excellence, and in <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mid-2020</FONT> we adjusted portions of our workforce where business had declined significantly and normal attrition was not sufficient. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During first quarter 2021, the cost saving impact of these actions totaled approximately $64&nbsp;million compared to
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> first quarter 2020, adjusted for pro forma full-quarter costs related to acquisitions. These cost savings were consistent with savings realized in second, third and fourth quarter 2020. Offsetting
these savings were severance and lease termination costs related to these actions. Thus far during second quarter 2021, we are holding most of our prior year cost savings. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We have $1.6&nbsp;billion of available liquidity; however, a return to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mid-2020</FONT> pandemic economic conditions may cause
our liquidity position to deteriorate. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">(2 of 14) </P>

</DIV></Center>

2021 and a net unrealized foreign exchange remeasurement gain of $12.4&nbsp;million in Q1 2020. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Interest and banking costs and</B>
<B>debt </B>- At March&nbsp;31, 2021, Gallagher had $4,373.0&nbsp;million of borrowings from private placements and no short-term borrowings under its line of credit facility. In addition, Gallagher had $151.3&nbsp;million outstanding under a
revolving loan facility that provides funding for premium finance receivables, which are fully collateralized by the underlying premiums held by insurance carriers, and as such are excluded from our debt covenant computations. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Clean energy -</B> Consists of the operating results related to our investments in clean coal production plants and royalty income from clean coal licenses
related to Chem-Mod LLC. Additional information regarding these results is available in the &#147;CFO Commentary&#148; at <U>ajg.com/IR</U>. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Acquisition costs -</B> Consists mostly of external professional fees and other due diligence costs related to acquisitions. On occasion, Gallagher enters
into forward currency hedges for the purchase price of committed, but not yet funded, acquisitions with funding requirements in currencies other than the U.S. dollar. The gains or losses, if any, associated with these hedge transactions is also
included. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Corporate </B>-<B> </B>Consists of overhead allocations mostly related to corporate staff compensation, other corporate level activities,
and net unrealized foreign exchange remeasurement. In addition, includes the tax expense related to partial taxation of foreign earnings, nondeductible executive compensation and entertainment expenses and the tax benefit from vesting of employee
equity awards. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Income Taxes </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gallagher allocates the
provision for income taxes to its Brokerage and Risk Management segments using the local country statutory rates. Gallagher&#146;s consolidated effective tax rate for the quarters ended March&nbsp;31, 2021 and 2020 was 3.6% and 0.2%, respectively,
which was lower than the statutory rate due to the production of IRC Section&nbsp;45 clean energy tax credits. In third quarter 2020, Gallagher increased its estimated U.K. effective income tax rate from 17.5% to 19%. </P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Webcast Conference Call </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gallagher will host a webcast conference call on Thursday, April&nbsp;29, 2021 at 5:15 p.m. ET/4:15 p.m. CT. To listen to this call, please go to
<U>ajg.com/IR</U>. The call will be available for replay at such website for at least 90 days. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>About Arthur J. Gallagher&nbsp;&amp; Co. </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Arthur J. Gallagher&nbsp;&amp; Co., an international insurance brokerage and risk management services firm, is headquartered in Rolling Meadows, Illinois, has
operations in 56 countries and offers client-service capabilities in more than 150 countries around the world through a network of correspondent brokers and consultants. </P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Information Regarding <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Measures </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In addition to reporting financial results in accordance with GAAP, this press release provides information regarding EBITDAC, EBITDAC margin, adjusted
EBITDAC, adjusted EBITDAC margin, diluted net earnings per share, as adjusted (adjusted EPS), adjusted revenue, adjusted compensation and operating expenses, adjusted compensation expense ratio, adjusted operating expense ratio and organic
revenue.&nbsp;These measures are not in accordance with, or an alternative to, the GAAP information provided in this press release.&nbsp;Gallagher&#146;s management believes that these presentations provide useful information to management, analysts
and investors regarding financial and business trends relating to Gallagher&#146;s results of operations and financial condition or because they provide investors with measures that our chief operating decision maker uses when reviewing the
company&#146;s performance. See further below for definitions and additional reasons each of these measures is useful to investors. Gallagher&#146;s industry peers may provide similar supplemental <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT>
information with respect to one or more of these measures, although they may not use the same or comparable terminology and may not make identical adjustments.&nbsp;The <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> information provided by
Gallagher should be used in addition to, but not as a substitute for, the GAAP information provided.&nbsp;As disclosed in its most recent Proxy Statement, Gallagher makes determinations regarding certain elements of executive officer incentive
compensation, performance share awards and annual cash incentive awards, partly on the basis of measures related to adjusted EBITDAC. Certain reclassifications have been made to the prior year amounts reported in this press release in order to
conform them to the current year presentation. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Adjusted <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> presentation</B> - Gallagher believes that
the adjusted <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> presentations of the current and prior period information presented in this earnings release provide stockholders and other interested persons with useful information regarding certain
financial metrics of Gallagher that may assist such persons in analyzing Gallagher&#146;s operating results as they develop a future earnings outlook for Gallagher. The <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax</FONT> amounts related to the
adjustments were computed using the normalized effective tax rate for each respective period. See pages&nbsp;13 and 14 for a reconciliation of the adjustments made to income taxes. </P>

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Earnings Measures </B></P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>EBITDAC</B> <B>and EBITDAC margin </B>- EBITDAC is net earnings before interest, income taxes, depreciation,
amortization and the change in estimated acquisition earnout payables and EBITDAC margin is EBITDAC divided by total revenues (for the Brokerage segment) and revenues before reimbursements (for the Risk Management segment). These measures for the
Brokerage and Risk Management segments provide a meaningful representation of Gallagher&#146;s operating performance for the overall business and provide a meaningful way to measure its financial performance on an ongoing basis.
</P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Adjusted EBITDAC</B> <B>and Adjusted EBITDAC Margin </B>- Adjusted EBITDAC is EBITDAC adjusted to exclude net
gains on divestitures, acquisition integration costs, workforce related charges, lease termination related charges, acquisition related adjustments and the period-over-period impact of foreign currency translation, as applicable and Adjusted EBITDAC
margin is Adjusted EBITDAC divided by total adjusted revenues (defined above). These measures for the Brokerage and Risk Management segments provide a meaningful representation of Gallagher&#146;s operating performance, and are also presented to
improve the comparability of our results between periods by eliminating the impact of the items that have a high degree of variability. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Adjusted EPS and Adjusted Net Earnings </B>- Adjusted net earnings have been adjusted to exclude the <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax</FONT> impact of net gains on divestitures, acquisition integration costs, the impact of foreign currency translation, workforce related charges, lease termination related charges, acquisition related adjustments
and effective income tax rate impact, as applicable. Adjusted EPS is Adjusted Net Earnings divided by diluted weighted average shares outstanding. This measure provides a meaningful representation of Gallagher&#146;s operating performance (and as
such should not be used as a measure of Gallagher&#146;s liquidity), and for the overall business is also presented to improve the comparability of our results between periods by eliminating the impact of the items that have a high degree of
variability. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Organic Revenues (a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measure)</B> - For the Brokerage segment, organic
change in base commission and fee revenues, supplemental revenues and contingent revenues exclude the first twelve months of such revenues generated from acquisitions and such revenues related to divested operations in each year
presented.&nbsp;These revenues are excluded from organic revenues in order to help interested persons analyze the revenue growth associated with the operations that were a part of Gallagher in both the current and prior periods.&nbsp;In addition,
organic change in base commission and fee revenues, supplemental revenues and contingent revenues excludes the period-over-period impact of foreign currency translation to improve the comparability of our results between periods by eliminating the
impact of the items that have a high degree of variability. For the Risk Management segment, organic change in fee revenues excludes the first twelve months of fee revenues generated from acquisitions in each year presented. In addition, change in
organic growth excludes the period-over-period impact of foreign currency translation to improve the comparability of our results between periods by eliminating the impact of the items that have a high degree of variability. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">These revenue items are excluded from organic revenues in order to determine a comparable, but <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP,</FONT> measurement
of revenue growth that is associated with the revenue sources that are expected to continue in the current year and beyond.&nbsp;Gallagher has historically viewed organic revenue growth as an important indicator when assessing and evaluating the
performance of its Brokerage and Risk Management segments.&nbsp;Gallagher also believes that using this <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measure allows readers of our financial statements to measure, analyze and compare the growth
from its Brokerage and Risk Management segments in a meaningful and consistent manner. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Reconciliation of
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Information Presented to GAAP Measures</B> - This press release includes tabular reconciliations to the most comparable GAAP measures, as follows: for EBITDAC (on pages&nbsp;11 and 12), for adjusted
revenues, adjusted EBITDAC and adjusted diluted net earnings per share (on page&nbsp;1), for organic revenue measures (on pages&nbsp;3 and 5, respectively, for the Brokerage and Risk Management segments), for adjusted compensation and operating
expenses and adjusted EBITDAC margin (on pages&nbsp;4, 5 and 6, respectively, for the Brokerage and Risk Management segments). </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">(10 of 14) </P>

</DIV></Center>
